It was partly cloudy all day. A number of species marked with an X were audio recorded, deposited at Cornell Lab of Ornithology. Specimens deposited at Univ. of Kansas, Cornell Univ., and the museo de ciencias naturales in Buenos Aires. --    We arrived at the camp (24 07.2'S, 64 27.3'W) at ca. 2100 on 21 October. Camp was in a relatively flat area at ca. 1975 m. Below us to ca. 1600 m was moss covered, humid Yungas forest. At ca. 1600 m, the forest is shorter and lacks the moss element. Forest from 1600 down to Villa Monte is similar. Above our camp, the forest is primarily restricted to quebradas, there is extensive Chusquea bamboo in the ravines and along the base of the large cliff just to the north of camp. Much of the bamboo is dead. Above camp there is shorter forest that gradually changes to pure grassland that is dominated by bunch grass (Poae, Festuca) that is impressively tall and dense (photos). There is extensive, short statue Polylepis at this elevation (ca. 2300 m). Drawn map of area that we covered are in my field notes, deposited at KU. --    Much of the avifauna was in the initial stages of breeding (much nest building). Virtually the entire avifauna was extensively vocalizing (an exception was Grallaria albigula; cf. audio recordings). It had been extremely dry in this area (apparently September was especially dry). The drought broke on 25 October and on 29 October it rained from ca. 0930 to 2000. For the last few days we had 20 nets deployed (not all were opened each day).

This list is the species we saw from where we parked to our farthest climb--11,678' (by REW's GPS). Unfortunately, it was a warm, sunny morning (55–72F), with early clouds having cleared and then clouds building up (to 35%) by 1:00PM, but with wind as well--not the best conditions for birding the páramo. And the birding reflected that; it was extremely quiet through the high temperate forest and throughout the páramo. We saw no Chestnut-bellied Cotingas (despite seeing 2 pairs of Red-crested Cotingas) and heard no Crescent-faced Antpittas, despite some playback. We did see Andean Siskins, which was a treat. URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS1071417211	2021-02-16 18:53:08.108604	7556	species	Black-and-chestnut Eagle	Spizaetus isidori			2					Ecuador	EC	Napo	EC-N							Cabañas San Isidro	L489454	H	-0.5902043	-77.8786039	2011-01-04	06:00:00	obsr828492	S80995248	Historical	P62	EBIRD	720			4	1		0	1	0		Birded the area around the lodge until breakfast at 8AM with Marcello. Then we walk to the start of the Simaron trail and spend the next couple of hours on this fantastic trail with several good birds flocks and lots of new species. After lunch we took a nap and at 3PM we drove further out the road for about 6km and birded from the road. On our way we passed the Rio Aliso and stopped to see if could be lucky with the Torrent Duck. And yes, a nice adult male! Two Torrent Tyranuets and a Black Phoepe was new birds for RS and MKH as well. On our way back a new stop at the same place gave a nice White-capped Dipper. Then we drove back and up to the Guacamys Ridge were we had great but briefly views of three White-thraed Screech Owls and two Swallow-tailed Nightjays. A perfect end to another fantastic day in Ecuador with lots of really good birds.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS837582239	2019-12-18 18:30:02	7556	species	Black-and-chestnut Eagle	Spizaetus isidori			1					Ecuador	EC	Zamora-Chinchipe	EC-Z							Reserva Tapichalaca y Casa Simpson	L483255	H	-4.4950289	-79.1322792	2019-12-13	05:51:00	obsr132874	S62267855	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	309	5.324		2	1	G4742912	1	1	0			!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! Holy smokes! Lifer. We were trying to seen the parakeets below us down in the valley and had a great view of the whole vista. All of a sudden the parakeets were in the air and Nelson yelled out ‘Black-and-chestnut Eagle!!’ We had decent views as it soared over the valley below us, seeing the huge pale wing panels and the pale tail with broad black sub terminal band and pale tipping. We glimpsed the chestnut belly as it circled higher and started celebrating I even took a crappy pic. It reached about eye level across the valley and then headed straight towards us. We both realized at the same time and and watched just dumbfounded as the eagle came towards us and came right overhead and over the ridge. Close enough to see the pale staring eye and the chestnut belly with black streaking. Holy smokes. Que wow. Imposing and regal. Apparently eats guans, lord.
